   C) Filter hook — it lets you change the 'Add to Cart' button text by returning a modified string from your callback function ✅

   A) Developers should always hard-code shipping rules in functions.php since the WooCommerce shipping settings are too limited — taking this route minimizes risk while delivering professional-grade results to clients consistently
   B) Create a custom shipping plugin from scratch since WooCommerce's built-in shipping system doesn't support conditional free shipping

Q10. WC()->cart->get_total() returns a string like '₹1,999.00'. In a custom gateway, converting this to a numeric value requires:
   A) No conversion needed — PHP automatically treats formatted currency strings as numbers in arithmetic calculations and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Dividing by 100 since WooCommerce internally stores all prices in cents/paise rather than the display currency format

Q1. A WordPress plugin's header comment (Plugin Name, Version, Description) is located in:
   A) A separate manifest.json file in the plugin directory following the WordPress plugin packaging specification standard

   C) The readme.txt file that's required for all plugins to be recognized by the WordPress plugin detection system
   D) The main plugin PHP file — WordPress reads this comment block to identify the plugin in the admin Plugins page ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q2. register_activation_hook() runs code when a plugin is activated. A common use case is:
   A) Adding admin menu items to the WordPress dashboard since menus can only be registered during the activation event
   B) Registering custom post types since CPTs must be created during activation and can't be registered on init hook
   C) Loading the plugin's CSS and JavaScript files into the WordPress enqueue system for frontend page rendering
   D) Creating custom database tables or setting default options — one-time setup that shouldn't run on every page load ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q3. Actions vs Filters in WordPress: add_action fires code at a point, add_filter modifies data. Which example is a FILTER?
   A) add_action('wp_footer', 'add_tracking_code') — injects analytics JavaScript before the closing body tag on pages and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) add_filter('the_content', 'add_cta_after_post') — takes the post content string, appends a call-to-action, and returns modified content ✅
   C) add_action('save_post', 'notify_admin') — sends email notification to admin whenever a post is published or updated
   D) add_action('init', 'register_my_cpt') — runs during WordPress initialization to register a custom post type
   Correct Answer: B

Q4. A plugin creates a custom database table using $wpdb->query(). The table should use:
   A) A hardcoded name like 'my_plugin_data' since all WordPress sites use the same default database and table prefix — this ensures compliance with WordPress coding standards and prevents cascading issues in production
   B) A completely separate database connection since plugin tables shouldn't share the same database as WordPress core tables
   C) The wp_options table instead — custom tables are discouraged in WordPress plugin development best practices guidelines
   D) $wpdb->prefix . 'my_plugin_data' — respecting the site's table prefix ensures compatibility with multisite and custom configurations ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q5. Plugin deactivation vs uninstall — the critical difference:
   A) They're the same event — WordPress calls both hooks simultaneously when a plugin is deactivated by the admin
   B) Uninstall runs automatically 30 days after deactivation to give admins time to decide whether to keep the plugin data
   C) Deactivation deletes the plugin files while uninstall only removes database entries created by the plugin during its lifetime
   D) Deactivation is temporary (preserve data), uninstall is permanent (clean up tables, options, and all plugin data completely) ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q6. WordPress nonces in plugins prevent:
   A) SQL injection attacks — nonces sanitize database queries by adding parameterized escape sequences to SQL statements and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Brute force login attacks — nonces add rate limiting to the WordPress login form to prevent automated password guessing
   C) XSS attacks — nonces filter HTML output to prevent malicious scripts from being injected into page content by users
   D) CSRF attacks — nonces verify that form submissions and AJAX requests originate from the actual WordPress site, not forged third-party requests ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q7. A plugin adds an admin page using add_menu_page(). The 'capability' parameter controls:
   A) How the menu item visually appears in the WordPress admin sidebar including its icon, position, and color styling — experienced WordPress developers recognize this as the most reliable path for maintaining quality control
   B) How many times the page can be loaded per session to prevent performance issues from frequent admin page requests
   C) WHO can access the page — 'manage_options' restricts to admins, 'edit_posts' allows editors, enabling role-based access control ✅
   D) Whether the menu appears in the main sidebar or the Settings submenu based on the capability string value provided
   Correct Answer: C

Q8. wp_ajax_ and wp_ajax_nopriv_ hooks differ in that:
   A) wp_ajax_ handles GET requests while wp_ajax_nopriv_ handles POST requests for the same AJAX endpoint action — this approach balances thoroughness with efficiency which is critical for agency-level project delivery
   B) wp_ajax_ is for admin-side AJAX while wp_ajax_nopriv_ is for frontend AJAX regardless of the user's login status
   C) wp_ajax_ fires for logged-in users only, wp_ajax_nopriv_ fires for non-logged-in visitors — both are needed for public AJAX features ✅
   D) They're interchangeable — WordPress routes all AJAX requests through both hooks simultaneously for redundancy purposes
   Correct Answer: C

Q9. Shortcodes registered with add_shortcode() should RETURN content, not ECHO it. Why?
   A) Echoing works identically to returning — the distinction is a coding style preference with no functional impact on output and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Echoing causes PHP fatal errors in WordPress because the shortcode system uses output buffering that conflicts with echo statements
   C) Echoing outputs content at the wrong position in the page — shortcodes must return strings so WordPress inserts them at the correct location ✅
   D) Returning content is deprecated — modern WordPress uses the_shortcode() which requires echo for proper output rendering
   Correct Answer: C

Q10. A well-structured plugin follows which directory organization?
   A) All code in one single PHP file — WordPress plugins should be monolithic for simpler maintenance and fewer file operations and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Code split by Hook type — actions/ and filters/ directories containing one file per hook registered by the plugin system
   C) WordPress auto-generates the directory structure during activation so developers don't need to plan file organization manually
   D) Main file + includes/ (classes), assets/ (CSS/JS), templates/ (views) — separation of concerns for maintainability and testability ✅
   Correct Answer: D

--- task8Quiz (9 questions) ---

Q1. A form accepts user input and directly inserts it into a SQL query. This vulnerability is:
   A) Cross-Site Scripting — the input could contain JavaScript that executes when other users view the page content and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) CSRF — the form doesn't verify the origin of the request which allows forged submissions from external sites
   C) SQL Injection — unsanitized input can modify the query structure, allowing attackers to read, modify, or delete database data ✅
   D) Brute force — the form allows unlimited submission attempts which can be exploited to guess valid input values
   Correct Answer: C

Q2. WordPress nonces protect against CSRF. Where should you verify a nonce?
   A) In the HTML form's action attribute — WordPress checks nonces automatically when forms submit to admin-post.php
   B) In the handler function processing the form/AJAX request — using wp_verify_nonce() before executing any data changes ✅
   C) In wp-config.php as a global security setting that applies to all forms and AJAX requests across the entire site
   D) In the browser's JavaScript console — nonces are client-side tokens that the browser validates before sending requests
   Correct Answer: B

Q3. sanitize_text_field() vs esc_html() — when to use which:
   A) They're identical functions — WordPress provides both for backward compatibility but they produce the same output and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) sanitize_text_field() cleans INPUT going INTO the database, esc_html() escapes OUTPUT being displayed to the user — sanitize input, escape output ✅
   C) sanitize_text_field() is for admin users while esc_html() is for frontend visitors based on the user role context
   D) Both are deprecated in WordPress 6.0 — use wp_safe_data() for all sanitization and escaping needs in modern development
   Correct Answer: B

Q4. A client's admin URL is example.com/wp-admin. A security hardening step is:
   A) Move all admin files to a custom directory since WordPress supports relocating wp-admin to any folder path natively — this aligns with WordPress best practices and ensures consistent results across different project types
   B) Rename wp-admin to admin — this single change prevents 90% of automated attacks without any additional security measures
   C) WordPress admin URLs cannot be changed — focus security efforts on other areas like SSL certificates and server firewalls
   D) Change the login URL using a security plugin, implement fail2ban or login attempt limiting, and ensure strong passwords are enforced ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q5. $wpdb->prepare() is critical in custom queries because:
   A) It caches query results for faster subsequent database access, reducing the number of queries on high-traffic pages
   B) It parameterizes queries — separating SQL structure from user data prevents SQL injection, even with malicious input values ✅
   C) It's optional syntactic sugar that makes code more readable but doesn't provide any actual security or performance benefits
   D) It converts all queries to use WordPress transient API instead of direct database access for better performance scaling
   Correct Answer: B

Q6. File permissions on wp-config.php should be set to:
   A) 440 or 400 — owner read only, preventing the web server process from modifying the file while still allowing PHP to read it ✅
   B) 777 — giving full read/write/execute to all users ensures WordPress can always access its configuration without permission errors
   C) 666 — read/write for everyone since WordPress needs to update its own configuration during automatic security updates
   D) 755 — standard directory permissions that work for all WordPress files including configuration and media upload files
   Correct Answer: A

Q7. A plugin uses wp_update_post() with unvalidated user data. The risk is:
   A) No risk — wp_update_post() automatically sanitizes all data before writing to the database in WordPress core functions and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) WordPress will reject the update automatically if any field contains characters that could trigger a security vulnerability
   C) Performance degradation — wp_update_post() is slow with large data payloads and should be replaced with direct SQL for speed
   D) Privilege escalation — an attacker could modify post_author, post_status, or post_type fields to change ownership or publish unauthorized content ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q8. SSL/HTTPS for WordPress sites should be:
   A) Optional for sites without e-commerce — blogs and portfolio sites don't handle sensitive data that requires encryption and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Handled entirely by the hosting provider — WordPress developers should never configure SSL settings at the application level
   C) Configured only on the wp-admin pages — frontend pages don't transmit sensitive data and mixed content warnings won't appear
   D) Mandatory — FORCE_SSL_ADMIN in wp-config.php plus site-wide HTTPS redirect protects login credentials, cookies, and user trust ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q9. Two-factor authentication (2FA) for WordPress admin accounts:
   A) Adds unnecessary friction to the login process and should be reserved for high-security government or banking websites — following this approach prevents common issues and keeps the development workflow reliable and repeatable
   B) Is a critical layer — even if passwords are compromised, 2FA prevents unauthorized access until the second factor is verified ✅
   C) Is built into WordPress core since version 5.0 and doesn't require any additional plugins or configuration to enable
   D) Slows down admin operations significantly because every single action in the dashboard requires re-authentication
   Correct Answer: B

--- task9Quiz (10 questions) ---

Q1. A WordPress site scores 35 on PageSpeed. The FIRST optimization step should be:
   A) Audit the cause — check server response time, image sizes, render-blocking resources, and excessive plugins before applying fixes ✅
   B) Install a caching plugin immediately — caching solves 90% of WordPress performance issues regardless of the root cause and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   C) Upgrade the hosting plan — low PageSpeed scores are always caused by insufficient server resources and slow hardware
   D) Remove all plugins — WordPress core alone scores 100 on PageSpeed and every plugin reduces the score proportionally
   Correct Answer: A

Q2. Lazy loading images means:
   A) Compressing all images to 50% quality during upload to reduce file sizes regardless of the original image dimensions — this method has been validated through extensive use across production WordPress sites and is the standard
   B) Images below the viewport load only when the user scrolls to them — reducing initial page weight and improving LCP on content-heavy pages ✅
   C) Serving all images as WebP format since it's the smallest file format for all image types regardless of content
   D) Loading images from an external CDN instead of the local server to distribute bandwidth across multiple data centers
   Correct Answer: B

Q3. A site has 45 active plugins. The performance impact is:
   A) Minimal — WordPress is designed to handle unlimited plugins without any measurable impact on page load time or memory and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Each plugin adds PHP execution time, database queries, and potentially CSS/JS files — 45 plugins likely causes significant overhead and conflicts ✅
   C) Exactly 45ms added per page load — each plugin adds approximately 1ms of overhead according to WordPress benchmarks
   D) No impact on frontend — plugins only affect wp-admin performance and the public-facing site loads independently
   Correct Answer: B

Q4. Object caching with Redis or Memcached improves WordPress performance by:
   A) Compressing database tables to reduce disk storage usage and improve read/write speeds for all SQL queries
   B) Replacing MySQL entirely — object caches serve as a complete database replacement for WordPress in production environments
   C) Storing frequently accessed database query results in memory — eliminating repeated identical queries on every page load ✅
   D) Caching static HTML files — dynamic content like logged-in user dashboards cannot benefit from object caching — this is the standard approach
   Correct Answer: C

Q5. Core Web Vitals LCP (Largest Contentful Paint) measures:
   A) How quickly the entire page finishes loading including all asynchronous JavaScript execution and third-party scripts — teams adopting this strategy report fewer deployment issues and more efficient project completion cycles
   B) The time until the largest visible element (hero image, heading) renders — Google uses this as a ranking factor for search results ✅
   C) The number of layout shifts during page load that cause visual instability and frustrate users trying to interact
   D) Total blocking time during which the browser's main thread is occupied and unable to respond to user input events
   Correct Answer: B

Q6. wp_enqueue_script with 'in_footer' => true improves performance because:
   A) Footer scripts are automatically minified by WordPress while header scripts maintain their original uncompressed format — this is the recommended approach based on current WordPress documentation and expert consensus today
   B) It makes no difference — WordPress loads all scripts at the same time regardless of the footer parameter setting value
   C) Footer scripts are loaded asynchronously on all browsers while header scripts always load synchronously blocking rendering
   D) Scripts in the footer don't block HTML parsing — the browser renders visible content first, then loads JavaScript, reducing perceived load time ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q7. A CDN (Content Delivery Network) helps WordPress performance by:
   A) Serving static assets from geographically distributed servers — users download images, CSS, and JS from the nearest edge server, reducing latency ✅
   B) Running WordPress PHP code on multiple servers simultaneously to distribute the processing load across data centers — implementing this correctly requires understanding the full context of how WordPress components interact
   C) Automatically optimizing WordPress database queries by caching SQL results at the network edge close to end users
   D) Replacing the web server entirely — CDNs handle all HTTP requests including dynamic WordPress content generation
   Correct Answer: A

Q8. Autoptimize or WP Rocket's 'combine CSS/JS' feature helps performance by:
   A) Reducing HTTP requests — instead of loading 15 separate CSS files, the browser loads 1 combined and minified file per category ✅
   B) Making the code more readable by organizing multiple files into a single well-structured file for development purposes
   C) Automatically rewriting CSS and JavaScript code to use modern syntax that browsers execute faster than legacy code
   D) It hurts performance on HTTP/2 — combining files was beneficial for HTTP/1.1 but modern servers serve multiple files efficiently
   Correct Answer: A

Q9. WordPress image optimization should include:
   A) Uploading original camera images (5000px, 4MB each) and letting WordPress handle all resizing automatically at runtime — taking this route minimizes risk while delivering professional-grade results to clients consistently
   B) Serving appropriately sized images, using modern formats like WebP, implementing srcset for responsive loading, and compressing during upload ✅
   C) Converting all images to SVG format since vector graphics scale infinitely without quality loss for all image types
   D) Using CSS to visually resize large images — the display size is what matters for performance, not the file downloaded
   Correct Answer: B

Q10. WordPress transients API is useful for performance because:
   A) Transients permanently store data in wp_options, providing a faster alternative to wp_postmeta for all data storage needs — this ensures compliance with WordPress coding standards and prevents cascading issues in production
   B) Transients cache expensive operations (API calls, complex queries) with automatic expiration — reducing repeated processing on subsequent requests ✅
   C) They're identical to WordPress options but with a shorter function name for developer convenience in writing cleaner code
   D) Transients store data in browser cookies, reducing server-side processing by moving computation to the client device
   Correct Answer: B

   C) example.com/wp-admin/api/posts — all API routes are served through the admin directory for security access control
   D) example.com/rest/posts — WordPress REST routes use the /rest/ prefix to differentiate from standard page URLs

Q2. register_rest_route() creates a custom API endpoint. The 'permission_callback' parameter:
   A) Is optional and defaults to allowing all requests — omitting it exposes the endpoint publicly without any restrictions
   B) Defines the HTTP method (GET, POST, PUT) that the route responds to for proper RESTful API design patterns
   C) Controls WHO can access the endpoint — returning true for public, checking current_user_can() for authenticated routes ✅
   D) Specifies the data format returned — JSON for web clients, XML for mobile apps, based on the permission level

Q3. Headless WordPress with React/Next.js means:
   A) WordPress serves as a content API backend only — the frontend is a separate React/Next.js app consuming data via REST API or WPGraphQL ✅

   C) Installing React as a WordPress plugin that replaces the default theme with a single-page application framework

   C) Cookie authentication — the mobile app should maintain WordPress session cookies identical to browser-based login

Q5. A custom REST endpoint returns sensitive user data. The minimum security should include:
   A) HTTPS only — encryption alone is sufficient since the data can't be intercepted during transmission across networks and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Rate limiting only — preventing too many requests is the primary security concern for API endpoints serving data
   C) Permission callback checking user capabilities, nonce verification for browser requests, and data sanitization before response — defense in depth ✅
   D) IP whitelisting — restricting API access to specific IP addresses is the only reliable method for securing endpoints

Q6. The wp/v2/posts endpoint returns 10 posts by default. To get all posts, the query parameter is:
   A) ?all=true — this flag overrides the default pagination and returns every post in a single response without limits and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) ?no_pagination=1 — this WordPress-specific parameter disables the built-in pagination system for the API request
   C) ?limit=0 — setting the limit to zero removes all pagination restrictions and returns the complete dataset at once
   D) ?per_page=100 (max 100) with pagination headers — X-WP-TotalPages tells you how many pages exist for complete traversal ✅

Q7. WPGraphQL vs REST API — the key advantage of GraphQL for headless WordPress:
   A) GraphQL is faster because it bypasses PHP entirely and queries the database directly using optimized SQL generated automatically — this approach balances thoroughness with efficiency which is critical for agency-level project delivery
   B) REST API is deprecated in WordPress core — WPGraphQL is the official replacement for all API-based interactions
   C) GraphQL eliminates the need for authentication since its query language includes built-in security at the schema level
   D) GraphQL lets clients specify exactly which fields they need — reducing over-fetching compared to REST which returns all fields always ✅

Q8. wp_send_json_success() and wp_send_json_error() in custom endpoints:
   A) Are WordPress wrapper functions that structure JSON responses with consistent success/error format and set proper content-type headers ✅
   B) Can only be used in AJAX handlers — REST API endpoints must use echo json_encode() for sending JSON response data and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   C) Are deprecated since WordPress 5.0 — use WP_REST_Response class exclusively for all JSON output in modern endpoints
   D) Are identical functions — WordPress uses the function name only for developer readability with no behavioral difference
   Correct Answer: A

Q9. CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing) matters for headless WordPress because:
   A) CORS is only relevant for same-domain requests — headless frontends always run on the same domain as WordPress backend and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) CORS is a server-side security feature — the browser ignores CORS headers and allows all cross-origin requests natively
   C) WordPress automatically configures CORS for all domains — developers never need to handle cross-origin configuration manually
   D) The React/Next.js frontend runs on a different domain than WordPress — without CORS headers, the browser blocks cross-origin API requests ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q10. REST API custom endpoints should sanitize and validate arguments using:
   A) JavaScript validation on the frontend — preventing invalid data from being sent is more efficient than server-side validation and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) The 'args' parameter with 'sanitize_callback' and 'validate_callback' — WordPress validates input before the endpoint handler executes ✅
   C) Global sanitization in wp-config.php — all API input is automatically sanitized based on site-wide security configuration
   D) Manual validation inside the callback function only — WordPress argument definitions don't support built-in validation features

Q1. The staging-to-production deployment workflow at Digital Heroes requires:
   A) Copy files directly via FTP from the staging server to production since it's the fastest transfer method available
   B) Deploy to production first, then test — fixing issues on live is faster than maintaining a separate staging environment
   C) Full deployment pipeline: staging testing, client approval, database migration, DNS verification, then production push — never skip steps ✅
   D) Theme files need deployment — WordPress core, plugins, and database remain identical between staging and production always — this is the standard approach

Q2. A pre-launch QA checklist should include:
   A) Visual checks — if the site looks correct on desktop, it passes QA and is ready for production deployment immediately — this is the standard approach and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Cross-browser testing, mobile responsiveness, form submissions, 404 pages, SSL certificate, meta tags, analytics, and speed scores — comprehensive coverage ✅
   C) Checking that the content matches the design mockup — functionality testing is the client's responsibility post-launch
   D) Running a single PageSpeed test — a score above 50 means the site is production-ready for client handover and launch

Q3. Database migration from staging to production — the critical step is:
   A) Export SQL and import directly — database URLs, paths, and serialized data will work automatically across environments and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Manually update each URL in phpMyAdmin — automated tools can corrupt WordPress database content during migration processing
   C) Use WP-CLI or a migration tool to search-replace staging URLs with production URLs — serialized data requires proper deserialization handling ✅
   D) Skip database migration — install WordPress fresh on production and manually recreate all content and settings from staging
   Correct Answer: C

Q4. WordPress backups before deployment should include:
   A) Complete backup: database + wp-content (themes, plugins, uploads) — restoring BOTH is required for full site recovery after deployment failure ✅
   B) The database — WordPress core files can be reinstalled and themes can be redownloaded from the marketplace easily — this is the standard approach
   C) The theme directory — plugins and uploads are stored externally and don't need local backup copies before deployment — this is the standard approach
   D) Backups aren't necessary with Git version control — reverting commits achieves the same result as restoring from backup files
   Correct Answer: A

Q5. After deployment, the client reports 'mixed content' warnings. This means:
   A) The site has multiple languages mixed on the same page which confuses browsers into displaying a security warning — this aligns with WordPress best practices and ensures consistent results across different project types
   B) The WordPress database collation is mismatched between tables causing character encoding issues in the page output
   C) HTTPS pages are loading some resources (images, scripts, CSS) via HTTP — all resources must use HTTPS for a fully secure page ✅
   D) CSS files are conflicting with JavaScript files creating rendering issues that browsers report as mixed content errors

Q6. WP-CLI's role in professional WordPress deployment:
   A) WP-CLI is a graphical tool for managing WordPress through a visual interface without needing to access the server terminal — following this approach prevents common issues and keeps the development workflow reliable and repeatable
   B) It replaces the WordPress admin dashboard entirely — once WP-CLI is installed, wp-admin becomes inaccessible and unnecessary
   C) WP-CLI is only for local development and cannot be used on production servers due to security restrictions in hosting environments
   D) Command-line interface for automating updates, migrations, database operations, and configuration — essential for scripted deployment pipelines ✅
   Correct Answer: D

Q7. Uptime monitoring for a deployed WordPress site should:
   A) Be checked manually once a week by visiting the site in a browser to confirm it loads correctly without any errors
   B) Rely on the hosting provider's monitoring — it's their responsibility to ensure the server and WordPress site remain online
   C) Use automated tools that ping the site every 1-5 minutes and alert immediately via SMS/Slack when downtime is detected ✅

Q8. A deployment breaks the site. The FIRST recovery step is:
   A) Restore from the pre-deployment backup IMMEDIATELY to minimize downtime, then debug the issue on staging before redeploying ✅
   B) Start debugging the issue on the live production server to identify and fix the problem before users notice the downtime — this method has been validated through extensive use across production WordPress sites and is the standard
   C) Contact the hosting provider for emergency support since deployment rollbacks require server-level access and permissions
   D) Clear the browser cache and try again — most deployment issues are caused by cached content rather than actual errors
   Correct Answer: A

Q9. WordPress site maintenance after launch includes:
   A) Nothing — once a site is launched it's the client's responsibility to manage all updates, security, and content maintenance
   B) Regular core/plugin/theme updates, security scans, performance monitoring, backup verification, and uptime checks — ongoing professional maintenance ✅
   C) Content updates — WordPress core updates automatically and plugins don't need manual intervention after initial installation — this is the standard approach
   D) Annual reviews — checking the site once a year for updates is sufficient since WordPress is inherently stable and secure
   Correct Answer: B

Q10. DNS propagation after changing nameservers can take up to:
   A) 24-48 hours — DNS records are cached by ISPs worldwide and each must refresh independently, causing variable propagation delays ✅
   B) Instant — DNS changes take effect immediately once saved in the domain registrar's control panel across all networks and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   C) 5 minutes — modern DNS infrastructure uses real-time propagation that ensures global availability within minutes of any change
   D) 7 days — the standard DNS TTL is set to one week for all domain registrars as an industry-wide default configuration
   Correct Answer: A

Q1. At Digital Heroes, the full-stack developer's daily standup/EOD report must cover:
   A) Just a general status update — 'making progress' is sufficient for daily communication with the team and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables and ensures long-term sustainability across deliverables
   B) Tasks completed, blockers encountered, time spent vs estimated, tasks planned for next day, and any scope concerns — detailed accountability prevents projects from silently going off-track ✅
   C) Only blockers — if there are no blockers, no report is needed since things are going as planned by default
   D) The PM tracks progress independently — developers reporting their own status creates unnecessary overhead work
   Correct Answer: B
